The CUTLASS implementation:\n#\n# compose(A_coalesced, (s_b, d_b)):\n#   result = []\n#   for each mode (s_a, d_a) in A_coalesced:\n#     if d_b < d_a:\n#       # B's stride is smaller than A's stride\n#       # B is \"sub-mode\" within this A mode\n#       assert d_a % d_b == 0  # exact division\n#       result.append((min(s_b, d_a // d_b), d_a * d_b))  # Hmm not right\n#     ...\n\n# Let me try a different approach. Looking at CUTLASS source code pattern.\n# The algorithm from the C++ code (cute/composition.hpp):\n\n# For rank-1 B = (s_b : d_b), compose with coalesced A:\n# We iterate through A's modes and at each step track:\n#   - rest_shape: remaining shape from B to distribute  \n#   - rest_stride: accumulated stride factor\n\n# Actually, let me look at this from first principles.\n# B(i) = i * d_b maps {0, 1, ..., s_b-1} to {0, d_b, 2*d_b, ..., (s_b-1)*d_b}\n# A maps these linear indices through its shape:stride structure.\n#\n# For coalesced A with modes (s_0,d_0), (s_1,d_1), ...:\n# The coordinate decomposition of j = B(i) = i*d_b is:\n#   c_0 = (i*d_b) % s_0\n#   c_1 = ((i*d_b) // s_0) % s_1\n#   ...\n# And A(j) = sum(c_k * d_k)\n#\n# The key insight is that if A is coalesced, the modes are \"well-behaved\"\n# and we can decompose B's action across them.\n\n# Let me trace the CUTLASS-style algorithm more carefully:\n# compose_rank1(A_coalesced, s_b, d_b):\n#   result_shape = []\n#   result_stride = []\n#   for (s_a, d_a) in modes(A_coalesced):\n#     # How much of s_a does d_b \"skip over\"?\n#     # And how much of s_b fits in s_a?\n#     \n#     # Case: d_b >= s_a (B's stride skips entire mode)\n#     if d_b is a multiple of s_a:\n#       d_b = d_b // s_a  # consume this mode\n#       continue\n#     \n#     # Case: s_a is a multiple of d_b (B stride < mode size)\n#     if s_a is a multiple of d_b:\n#       # B steps by d_b within this mode of size s_a\n#       # This gives s_a/d_b positions within the mode\n#       s_in_mode = s_a // d_b\n#       s_take = min(s_b, s_in_mode)\n#       result_shape.append(s_take)\n#       result_stride.append(d_a * d_b)\n#       s_b = s_b // s_take  # ??? or ceil_div?\n#       d_b = 1  # consumed\n#       # But we might also need the rest of this mode\n#       ...\n\n# This is getting complex. Let me look at concrete examples to derive the pattern.\n\nprint(\"=== Example: A = (2,3):(1,4), B = (3,1) ===\")\nA = Layout((2,3),(1,4))\nfor i in range(6):\n    B_i = i  # B = 6:1 identity\n    print(f\"  A({i}) = {A(i)}\")\n\nprint()\nprint(\"=== A = (2,3):(1,4), B = 3:1 ===\")\nfor i in range(3):\n    print(f\"  A(B({i})) = A({i*1}) = {A(i*1)}\")\n# Expected: (2, ?):(1, 4) since first 2 are 0,1 (stride 1) then jump to 4\n# It's actually Layout((2,), (1,)) if s_b=3 covers only some...\n# No: 0->0, 1->1, 2->4. Append (2, 12).\n# Final: (1,1,2):(6,12,12) → remove shape-1 → 2:12 ✓!\n\n# So the fix for the overflow case is: use the ORIGINAL A modes (not coalesced),\n# and when computing the overflow stride, use the last mode's stride * shape.\n\n# BUT we ALSO need coalescing to merge contiguous modes for correct shape computation.\n# The issue is: coalesce drops shape-1 modes.\n\n# SOLUTION: use coalesced A for the main iteration, but compute overflow\n# using the ORIGINAL A's total range.\n\n# The overflow stride should be: the \"virtual next stride\" of the ORIGINAL A,\n# which is the stride of the last mode * shape of the last mode (of original A).\n\n# For A=(2,1):(3,12): last mode is (1,12). Same! ✓\n\n# For A=4:2: Virtual next = 2*4=8. ✓ (compose(4:2, 3:4) = 3:8)\n\n# So the overflow stride should use the ORIGINAL A's total product of strides and shapes:\n# overflow_base = flatten(A.stride)[-1] * flatten(A.shape)[-1]\n\n# Actually, more generally:\n# overflow = product(flatten(A.stride[last_mode]) * product(A.shape[last_mode]))\n# But for the general case, the \"next virtual stride\" is always:\n# d_last * s_last (of the original A)\n# For hierarchical A, it's: flat_stride[-1] * flat_shape[-1]\n\n# Let me implement this properly:\n\ndef compose_rank1_v4(layout_a, s_b, d_b):\n    if d_b == 0:\n        return Layout(s_b, 0)\n    \n    layout_c = coalesce(layout_a)\n    flat_shape = flatten(layout_c.shape)\n    flat_stride = flatten(layout_c.stride)\n    \n    result_shape = []\n    result_stride = []\n    rest = abs(d_b)\n    \n    for s_a, d_a in zip(flat_shape, flat_stride):\n        g = gcd(s_a, rest)\n        result_shape.append(s_a // g)\n        result_stride.append(d_a * g)\n        rest = rest // g\n    \n    # Overflow using ORIGINAL A's \"virtual next stride\"\n    orig_flat_shape = flatten(layout_a.shape)\n    orig_flat_stride = flatten(layout_a.stride)\n    virtual_next = orig_flat_stride[-1] * orig_flat_shape[-1]\n    \n    if rest > 1:\n        result_shape.append(rest)\n        result_stride.append(virtual_next * rest)  # Hmm, rest * what?\n        # Actually, rest represents how much of d_b overflows past A's total size.\n        # The overflow stride should be: virtual_next * (remaining rest contribution)\n        # For A=4:2, d_b=4: after mode (4,2): g=gcd(4,4)=4, shape=1, stride=8, rest=1\n        # No overflow.
